# Voyager - Getting Setup on [Gaudi2](https://habana.ai/products/gaudi2/)

[Habana Labs](https://habana.ai) has provided us with access to a Gaudi2 compute node available on the [Intel Developer Cloud (IDC)](https://cloud.intel.com) to evaluate its performance.

```
mkandes@hardtack:~$ ssh -J guest@146.152.232.8 sdp@100.82.255.110
```

Let's start by gathering some general system specs --- so that we know what we're working with here. In addition to running `hl-smi`, here are some other (standard) system commands we might typically use to collect additional information when running benchmarks.

```
sdp@sdsc-gaudi2:~$ cat /etc/os-release 
NAME="Ubuntu"
VERSION="20.04.6 LTS (Focal Fossa)"
ID=ubuntu
ID_LIKE=debian
PRETTY_NAME="Ubuntu 20.04.6 LTS"
VERSION_ID="20.04"
HOME_URL="https://www.ubuntu.com/"
SUPPORT_URL="https://help.ubuntu.com/"
BUG_REPORT_URL="https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/"
PRIVACY_POLICY_URL="https://www.ubuntu.com/legal/terms-and-policies/privacy-policy"
VERSION_CODENAME=focal
UBUNTU_CODENAME=focal
sdp@sdsc-gaudi2:~$
```

Okay, that's probably too much information for this first note. But I cannot promise that these notes will be nice and neat, or even comprehensible. My only hope is that they will be easily searchable, long-term. With that said, let's get back to getting setup on this Gaudi2 compute node.

One initial problem is that we currently have only one compute node with a single user account and HOME directory. But we have many people on the team who would like to run some benchamrks on the system while we have it --- and presumably, on the Gaudi2 cluster as well when ready. 


Let's see if we can setup indiviudal user accounts to make this a bit less painful --- and this would avoid giving everyone `sudo` access to the system, which could become a mess. 

```
sdp@sdsc-gaudi2:~$ sudo useradd --create-home mkandes
sdp@sdsc-gaudi2:~$ ls -lahtr /home/
total 16K
drwxr-xr-x 19 root    root    4.0K Oct 27 21:29 ..
drwxr-xr-x  4 sdp     sdp     4.0K Oct 27 21:38 sdp
drwxr-xr-x  2 mkandes mkandes 4.0K Oct 31 23:05 mkandes
drwxr-xr-x  4 root    root    4.0K Oct 31 23:05 .
sdp@sdsc-gaudi2:~$
```

 So far, so good. Now, let's drop in a public key.


Now, can I use the jumphost with this new user account?

```
mkandes@hardtack:~$ ssh -J guest@146.152.232.8 mkandes@100.82.255.110

mkandes@hardtack:~$
```

Maybe a permissions issue?


Yes! But unfortuantely, Habana still appears to be very cloud-forward with their assumptions.

Let's go ahead and simply attempt to run some initial benchmark tests from my new user account. But first, let's install Singularity (or Apptainer) as another option (to Docker) for people to run Habana's standard containers (or their own). More people running their own tests on this evaluation node may be more familiar with using Singularity than Docker --- most are only using Docker indirectly via K8s on Voyager.

Unfortuantely, it looks like this may affect the Docker installation already available on the node, which is why I declined to install of `runc` above. Let's hold off on trying the Singularity approach for now. It should also be noted that the Intel support team warned us not to delete this instance from IDC. Are we allowed to reboot the system? Maybe I should check with them first before making any other significant changes to the base operating system environment.  

I cannot `docker pull` the latest [prebuilt](https://docs.habana.ai/en/latest/shared/Pull_Prebuilt_Container_Bare_Metal.html) TensorFlow container from the Habana vault from my new user account.
```
kandes@sdsc-gaudi2:~$ docker pull vault.habana.ai/gaudi-docker/1.12.1/ubuntu22.04/habanalabs/tensorflow-installer-tf-cpu-2.13.0:latest
permission denied while trying to connect to the Docker daemon socket at unix:///var/run/docker.sock: Post "http://%2Fvar%2Frun%2Fdocker.sock/v1.24/images/create?fromImage=vault.habana.ai%2Fgaudi-docker%2F1.12.1%2Fubuntu22.04%2Fhabanalabs%2Ftensorflow-installer-tf-cpu-2.13.0&tag=latest": dial unix /var/run/docker.sock: connect: permission denied
```
However, I have no problem pulling in the container from the default `sdp` user account.
```

```
Let's try adding `mkandes` to the `docker` group. See this [note from Digital Ocean](https://www.digitalocean.com/community/questions/how-to-fix-docker-got-permission-denied-while-trying-to-connect-to-the-docker-daemon-socket). 
```
sdp@sdsc-gaudi2:~$ sudo usermod -aG docker mkandes
sdp@sdsc-gaudi2:~$ groups mkandes
mkandes : mkandes docker
sdp@sdsc-gaudi2:~$
```
That did the trick.
```
mkandes@sdsc-gaudi2:~$ groups
mkandes docker
mkandes@sdsc-gaudi2:~$ docker images -a
```

Here we go. Not too hard. See the Docker documenation on [Bind mounts](https://docs.docker.com/storage/bind-mounts/).
```
mkandes@sdsc-gaudi2:~$ docker run -it --runtime=habana -e HABANA_VISIBLE_DEVICES=all -e OMPI_MCA_btl_vader_single_copy_mechanism=none --cap-add=sys_nice --net=host --mount type=bind,source="${PWD}",destination="${PWD}" vault.habana.ai/gaudi-docker/1.12.0/ubuntu20.04/habanalabs/tensorflow-installer-tf-cpu-2.13.0:latest
 * Starting OpenBSD Secure Shell server sshd                             [ OK ] 
root@sdsc-gaudi2:/# ls /home/mkandes
software
root@sdsc-gaudi2:/# ls /home/mkandes/software/tensorflow/benchmarks/custom/training/vision/image-classification/scnn/cifar/
htf2-train-scnn-cifar.py  hvd-htf2-train-scnn-cifar.py  tf2-train-scnn-cifar.py
oot@sdsc-gaudi2:/# cd /home/mkandes/software/tensorflow/benchmarks/custom/training/vision/image-classification/scnn/cifar/
root@sdsc-gaudi2:/home/mkandes/software/tensorflow/benchmarks/custom/training/vision/image-classification/scnn/cifar# touch test.txt
root@sdsc-gaudi2:/home/mkandes/software/tensorflow/benchmarks/custom/training/vision/image-classification/scnn/cifar# vi test.txt

Hello, this is my first Docker bind mount.
```

But we're probably going to have a `root:root` ownership problem with any directories and/or files created from within the Docker container(s). Hmmm. Maybe not?

It doesn't look like it from the latest documentation on [Porting a Simple TensorFlow Model to Gaudi](https://docs.habana.ai/en/latest/TensorFlow/Migration_Guide/Porting_Simple_TensorFlow_Model_to_Gaudi.html).
